2:31:2008:0:14:72:455:700:12:Times:12:Times:F:Macroprudential FX Regulations: Shifting the Snowbanks of FX Vulnerability?
2:32:2083:14:14:72:414:686:12:Times:12:Times:F:Toni Ahnert, Kristin Forbes, Christian Friedrich, and Dennis Reinhardt
2:33:2153:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:F:NBER Working Paper No. 25083
2:34:2181:14:14:72:150:658:12:Times:12:Times:F:September 2018
2:35:2195:14:28:72:226:644:12:Times:12:Times:F:JEL No. F32,F34,G15,G21,G28
2:36:2222:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:37:2230:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:F:Can  macroprudential  foreign  exchange  (FX)  regulations  on  banks  reduce  the  financial  and 
2:38:2329:14:14:72:545:574:12:Times:12:Times:F:macroeconomic vulnerabilities  created  by  borrowing  in  foreign  currency?  To  evaluate  the 
2:39:2425:14:14:72:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:F:effectiveness  and  unintended consequences  of  macroprudential  FX  regulations,  we  develop  a 
2:40:2523:14:14:72:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:F:parsimonious model of bank and market lending in domestic and foreign currency and derive four 
2:41:2617:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:F:predictions. We confirm these predictions using a rich dataset of macroprudential FX regulations. 
2:42:2714:14:14:72:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:F:These empirical tests show that FX regulations:(1) are effective in terms of reducing borrowing in 
2:43:2812:14:14:72:545:504:12:Times:12:Times:F:foreign currency by banks; (2) have the unintended consequence of simultaneously causing firms 
2:44:2906:14:14:72:546:490:12:Times:12:Times:F:to increase FX debt issuance; (3) reduce the sensitivity of banks to exchange rate movements, but 
2:45:3003:14:14:72:542:476:12:Times:12:Times:F:(4) are less effective at reducing the sensitivity of corporates and the broader financial market to
2:46:3102:14:14:72:542:462:12:Times:12:Times:F:exchange  rate  movements.  As  a  result,  FX  regulations  on  banks appear  to  be  successful  in
2:47:3202:14:14:72:543:448:12:Times:12:Times:F:mitigating the vulnerability of banks to exchange rate movements and the global financial cycle,
2:48:3297:14:28:72:399:434:12:Times:12:Times:F:but partially shift the snowbank of FX vulnerability to other sectors.
2:49:3367:28:14:72:131:406:12:Times:12:Times:F:Toni Ahnert

2:56:3488:28:14:72:141:294:12:Times:12:Times:F:Kristin Forbes
2:57:3502:14:14:72:239:280:12:Times:12:Times:F:MIT Sloan School of Management

3:74:3828:0:30:102:196:706:122:Georgia:122:Georgia:A:I. Introduction 
3:75:3842:30:19:102:528:676:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:The  global  financial  crisis  has  prompted  renewed  interest  in  tools  to  reduce 
3:76:3930:19:19:75:528:657:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:macroeconomic and  financial vulnerabilities,  strengthen  financial  systems,  and  improve 
3:77:4023:19:19:75:528:638:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:country resilience. A key component of this   strategy is greater use of macroprudential tools — 
3:78:4120:19:18:75:528:619:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:such as countercyclical capital buffers, tighter reserve ratios, leverage ratios, and restrictions 
3:79:4219:18:19:75:528:601:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:on  loan-to-value  and  debt-to-income  ratios.  Several  papers  have  analyzed  the  use  and 
3:80:4315:19:19:75:548:582:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:effectiveness of many of these tools.1 One    type of tool, macroprudential foreign exchange (FX) 
3:81:4412:19:19:75:528:563:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations, however,  has    received  less  attention,  despite  the  long-standing  research 
3:82:4508:19:30:75:412:544:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:documenting the vulnerabilities associated with currency mismatch.  
3:83:4575:30:19:102:528:514:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:This paper seeks to fill this gap. It   provides a detailed assessment of macroprudential 
3:84:4665:19:19:75:528:495:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations on the use of foreign currencies by banks, including theoretical predictions of how 
3:85:4761:19:19:75:528:476:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:they could work and then empirical assessments of their direct and unintended consequences 
3:86:4852:19:18:75:528:457:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:using  a  rich  new  dataset.  We  find that    macroprudential  FX policies  are  effective  in 
3:87:4949:18:19:75:528:439:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:accomplishing their primary goal of reducing bank exposure to for eign currency risk. But do 
3:88:5042:19:19:75:528:420:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:they simply shift the risk elsewhere—similar to “shifting a snowbank” (a pile of snow) from 
3:89:5134:19:19:75:528:401:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:one place to another? We find some evidence of a “shifting snowbank” effect, as reduced FX 
3:90:5225:19:18:75:528:382:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:lending from banks causes some firms to  increase  FX debt issuance to investors. This shifting 
3:91:5321:18:19:75:528:364:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:is only partial, however, so that aggregate exposure to FX debt    declines. Our results also show 
3:92:5420:19:19:75:544:345:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:that these FX  regulations reduce the sensitivity of banks to currency movements, but   are less 
3:93:5517:19:19:75:527:326:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:successful at reducing the sensitivity of the corporate sector and the   broader economy. As a 
3:94:5612:19:18:75:528:307:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:result, although macroprudential FX regulations can    substantially improve the resilience of 
3:95:5707:18:19:75:528:289:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:the banking sector to the global financial cycle  , the benefits to the broader economy may be 
3:96:5802:19:19:75:528:270:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:more moderate,  as some vulnerability shifts to other sectors that    may be less informed and 
3:97:5897:19:31:75:248:251:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:make less efficient lending choices. 
3:98:5934:31:18:102:528:220:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Exposure to foreign currency borrowing and currency mismatch has  been a habitual 
3:99:6016:18:19:75:530:202:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:concern, especially in emerging markets. Foreign currency exposure can increase a country’s  
3:100:6109:19:19:75:528:183:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:vulnerability to sudden stops, currency depreciations, and financial and banking crises, as well 
3:101:6206:19:19:75:528:164:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:as  limit    the ability of the exchange rate and monetary policy to respond to shocks (Rey, 2013). 
3:102:6306:19:18:75:528:145:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Despite these concerns, foreign currency exposure has continued to increase—especially in 
3:103:6396:18:32:75:525:127:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:the corporate and household sector.2 For example, over our sample period from the mid-
3:104:6482:32:8:228:231:95:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
3:105:6537:8:11:70:414:87:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:1 Cerutti et al. (2015) and Forbes (2018) are recent surveys of this extensive literature.  
3:106:6627:11:0:70:502:76:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:2 See   Acharya et al. (2015  ),  Bruno and Shin (2016  ),  Chui et al. (2014  , 2016), and Du and Schreger ( 2016  ). 
4:107:6747:0:18:75:528:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:1990s through end-2014, total FX borrowing in international debt securities and bank loans 
4:108:6838:18:19:75:528:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:more than tripled to about $12 trillion USD. FX borrowing has continued to grow since the 
4:109:6928:19:19:75:528:669:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:2008 crisis   —with    cross   -border FX borrowing in international debt securities and FX loans 
4:110:7026:19:19:75:528:650:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:increasing by  around $ 2.5   trillion USD    between 2009 and 2015—a sharp contrast to almost 
4:111:7121:19:18:75:529:631:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:no change in comparable cross-border borrowing in local currency over the same period. 
4:112:7208:18:19:75:528:613:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Concerns about the macroeconomic and financial risks related to FX exposure have increased 
4:113:7299:19:31:75:321:594:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:interest in using macroprudential FX regulations.  
4:114:7350:31:19:102:529:563:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Evaluating the effects  of macroprudential FX measures has been challenging, however, 
4:115:7436:19:18:75:529:544:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:partly due to insufficient data   linked to the limited experience with these tools until recently, 
4:116:7536:18:19:75:528:526:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:and  partly  due  to  identification  challenges  related  to  macroprudential regulations  being 
4:117:7634:19:19:75:528:507:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:introduced  as  a  response  to  financial  and  macroeconomic  developments.3  An  evaluation 
4:118:7729:19:19:75:528:488:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:should assess not only the direct effects of these measures on the intended sector of the 
4:119:7819:19:18:75:528:469:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:economy (such as banks), but also any spillovers or leakages as firms, banks, and    other    entities 
4:120:7921:18:19:75:528:451:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:respond to the regulations. These types of unintended consequences have been highlighted in 
4:121:8013:19:19:75:529:432:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:analyses of other types of macroprudential regulations and capital controls.4 If these leakages 
4:122:8109:19:19:75:529:413:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:and    subst  itution effects occur, can these macroprudential policies achieve their primary goal 
4:123:8208:19:30:75:374:394:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:of reducing aggregate country vulnerability to currency risk?  
4:124:8270:30:19:102:528:364:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:This paper attempts to tackle these challenges in an assessment of the direct and indirect 
4:125:8360:19:19:75:528:345:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:effects of macroprudential FX regulations on banks and the broader economy. We develop a 
4:126:8449:19:19:75:528:326:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:parsimonious  model  of  bank  versus  market  lending,  building  on  the  seminal work  of 
4:127:8542:19:18:75:528:307:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Holmstrom and Tirole (1997), but adding the dimension that lending and borrowing is also 
4:128:8631:18:19:75:532:289:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:differentiated  between domestic and foreign currencies . Domestic firms seek funding from 
4:129:8722:19:19:75:531:270:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:lenders,  but have private information about their productivity. Banks can screen firms at a 
4:130:8815:19:19:75:528:251:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:cost and identify unproductive, low-productivity, and high-productivity firms, while market 
4:131:8907:19:18:75:528:232:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:investors can  only  lend  indiscriminately.  Funding  in  foreign  currency  is  cheaper than  in 
4:132:9006:18:19:75:529:214:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:domestic currency,  but subject to exchange rate risk. When the domestic currency depreciates, 
4:133:9101:19:19:75:528:195:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:low -productivity firms and their associated banks default. Macroprudential FX regulation 
4:134:9191:19:19:76:528:176:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:increases  banks’  cost  of  funding  in  foreign  currency  (if the  regulation  is  a liability-side 
4:135:9294:19:32:76:528:157:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:measure) or the equilibrium lending rate to firms (if an asset-side measure). Banks stop 
4:136:9383:32:8:228:231:125:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
4:137:9438:8:12:70:537:117:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:3  Papers  which  include  some discussion of  macroprudential  FX  regulations  as  part  of  their  broader  analyses  of 
4:138:9562:12:11:70:537:105:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f5:?:macroprudential tools are: Nier et al. (2011), Cerutti et al. (2015), Vandenbussche et al. (2015  ), and Avdjiev et al. 
4:139:9681:11:10:70:537:94:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:(2016b). Two papers which focus on FX regulations are  De Crescenzio et al. (2017) and Aguirre and Repetto (2017), 
4:140:9796:10:8:70:486:84:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:but neither consider the leakages, broader effects on the economy,  or sensitivity to currency movements. 
4:141:9901:8:0:70:279:76:36:g_d0_f2:99:g_d0_f2:?:4 See  Agénor and da Silva (2017) for a recent survey. 
5:142:9957:0:18:75:551:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:lending to low-productivity firms, which respond by shi  fting  some of their    foreign currency 
5:143:10055:18:19:75:528:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:borrowing from banks to investors.  Total factor productivity declines, as FX   lending shifts to 
5:144:10153:19:19:75:528:669:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:investors (who    cannot screen) and a share of FX  lending shifts to less productive firms. The 
5:145:10250:19:19:75:531:650:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:overall  impact  on  welfare  is  ambiguous and  reflects  a tradeoff  between  two  forces:  FX 
5:146:10347:19:18:75:528:631:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulation provides the benefit of reducing the social cost of bank failure after depreciations 
5:147:10443:18:31:75:459:613:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:at  the cost of reducing output due to the less efficient allocation of FX lending.  
5:148:10528:31:19:102:538:582:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Our simple framework yields four  testable implications for how macroprudential FX 
5:149:10611:19:19:75:528:563:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations affect bank and corporate borrowing, cross-border capital flows, FX exposure in 
5:150:10703:19:18:75:528:544:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:different  sectors  of  the  economy,  and  macroeconomic  vulnerability  to  exchange  rate 
5:151:10796:18:19:75:528:526:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:move   ments. After an increase in macroprudential FX regulations: (1) banks borrow and lend 
5:152:10889:19:19:75:528:507:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:less in foreign currency ( with no change in their borrowing in local currency); (2) firms shift 
5:153:10986:19:19:75:528:488:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:away from bank borrowing and increase  their FX borrowing from market investors (with no 
5:154:11075:19:18:76:532:469:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:in crease in firm and bank non-FX borrowing from investors);  (3) banks are less exposed to 
5:155:11167:18:19:76:528:451:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:exchange rate movements; and (4) firms experience some reduction in their exposure to 
5:156:11253:19:31:76:323:432:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:exchange rate movements, but less than for banks. 
5:157:11303:31:19:103:528:401:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:To  test  these four    predictions, we  build  a rich  data  set  on  macroprudential  FX 
5:158:11394:19:18:75:528:382:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations,  defined  as  policies  directed  at  the  broader  financial  system  (compared  to 
5:159:11492:18:19:75:538:364:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:prudential regulations that target individual institutions) and that are  based on the currency 
5:160:11588:19:19:76:536:345:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:denomination  of  the  capital  transaction. The    dataset is  based  on  four  sources  that  each 
5:161:11689:19:19:76:529:326:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:document and measure macroprudential FX regulations in different contexts or for different 
5:162:11780:19:18:76:529:307:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:countries: Shim et al. (2013  ),  Vandenbussche et al. (2015  ),  Cerutti et al. (2017) and    Reinhardt 
5:163:11884:18:19:76:528:289:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:and  Sowerbutts (2018) .  Our   resulting data  set includes  information  on  macroprudential 
5:164:11979:19:19:76:574:270:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations in 48 countries over the  period 1995  -2014. It    has    broader country and period 
5:165:12077:19:19:76:528:251:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:coverage of macroprudential FX regulations, as well as a  more detailed categorization of 
5:166:12167:19:30:76:351:232:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:different types of regulations, than previously available.  
5:167:12226:30:19:103:528:202:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:The empirical analysis confirms the four testable implications of the model, as well as 
5:168:12314:19:19:76:528:183:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:provides additional details on how tighter macroprudential FX regulations affect (or do not 
5:169:12406:19:19:76:528:164:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:affect)  different  types  of  cross-border  capital  flows,  banks,  and  sensitivity  to  currency 
5:170:12507:19:18:76:528:145:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:movements. These  results  suggest  that  macroprudential FX  regulations  on  banks are 
5:171:12595:18:19:75:528:127:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:successful in accomplishing their direct goals —    of reducing the FX exposure of banks and 
5:172:12687:19:19:75:528:108:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:sensitivity of banks to currency movements. There is also some evidence that this occurs 
5:173:12776:19:0:75:528:89:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:because the regulations reduce domestic lending in FX, increase the average rate at which 
6:174:12868:0:18:75:528:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:banks lend, and reduce the share of banks’ non-performing loans, partly by reducing the 
6:175:12956:18:19:75:528:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:number of entities to which they lend. The FX regulations, however, also appear to have the 
6:176:13048:19:19:75:528:669:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:unintended consequence of causing companies to   partially shift   their    FX funding toward 
6:177:13141:19:19:75:529:650:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:international debt issuance, thereby mitigating the reduction in the aggregate exposure of the 
6:178:13236:19:18:75:528:631:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:economy to FX risk.  These results are robust to a series of sensitivity tests, including attempts 
6:179:13335:18:31:75:508:613:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:to control for any potential endogeneity in the country’s decision to adjust FX measures.  
6:180:13425:31:19:102:528:582:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:The   magnitudes of the est imates also    suggest that these direct and indirect effects of 
6:181:13518:19:19:75:528:563:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:macroprudential FX regulations are meaningful. A  tightening of FX  regulations causes banks 
6:182:13611:19:18:75:528:544:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:to reduce their cross-border borrowing in FX by about a third,  a reduction equivalent to about 
6:183:13707:18:19:75:528:526:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:0.5%  -0.7 %  of  GDP.  For   major  emerging  markets,  such  as  Brazil or  Indonesia,  this  is 
6:184:13806:19:19:75:547:507:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:equivalent to reducing cross-border bank    FX borrowing by more than half.    At the same time, 
6:185:13903:19:19:75:528:488:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:corporates increase FX debt issuance by  about 10% of median annual FX debt issuance for the 
6:186:13996:19:18:75:528:469:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:full sample, equivalent to a 15%-20% increase in FX corporate debt issuance for emerging 
6:187:14085:18:19:75:528:451:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:markets such as Brazil and Indonesia. Combining these various estimates suggests that FX 
6:188:14174:19:19:75:525:432:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations still   cause a meaningful reduction in the aggregate FX borrowing of the country—
6:189:14268:19:19:75:529:413:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:as the reduction in cross-border FX bank borrowing is substantially greater than the increase 
6:190:14362:19:18:75:533:394:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:in FX corporate debt issuance—but that 10% -16% of the aggregate FX exposure shifts from 
6:191:14451:18:19:75:528:376:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:banks to other sectors (such as investors  and non-bank financial institutions). The    effects are 
6:192:14551:19:31:75:435:357:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:larger if the FX measures focus on bank liabilities instead of bank assets.   
6:193:14629:31:19:102:528:326:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Our    results  have several imp  ortant  implications.  They  support  a  growing  body  of 
6:194:14722:19:18:75:529:307:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:research showing that macroprudential regulations can be effective at accomplishing their 
6:195:14812:18:19:75:554:289:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:direct  goals5—in  this  case significantly reduc   ing   the  FX  exposure  of  banks  to  currency 
6:196:14913:19:19:75:528:270:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:movements. This  result is particularly relevant for the debate on how to address long-standing 
6:197:15009:19:19:75:528:251:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:concerns about vulnerabilities related to foreign currency borrowing and currency mismatch.6 
6:198:15101:19:18:75:528:232:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:The  se vulnerabilities have    prompted some countries to consider the use of capital controls. 
6:199:15198:18:19:75:529:214:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Our    results  suggest  that any  such countries could     instead consider  macroprudential  FX 
6:200:15296:19:19:75:528:195:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations—especially  countries  for  which  capital  controls  (but  not  macroprudential  FX 
6:201:15393:19:40:75:528:176:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations) are illegal, such as in the European Economic Area and in some    trade agreements. 
6:202:15489:40:8:228:231:136:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
6:203:15544:8:13:70:537:128:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:5 Prominent examples include: Dell’Ariccia et al. (2011   ),  Ostry et al. ( 2012  ), Kuttner and Shim (2013), Akinci and 
6:204:15666:13:10:70:547:115:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:Olmstead-Rumsey (2015  ),  Bruno et al. (2015  ),  Cerutti et al. (2015  ), Forbes et al. (2015), Vandenbussche et al. (2015  ), 
6:205:15795:10:8:70:202:105:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:and Beirne and Friedrich (2017). 
6:206:15827:8:13:70:537:97:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:6  For  discussions  of  “original  sin”  and  vulnerabilities  related  to  foreign  currency  exposure  and  mismatch,  see 
6:207:15953:13:10:70:555:84:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:Eichengreen and Hausmann (1999), Bordo and Meissner  ( 2005   ), Desai  et al. ( 2008   ),  Zettelmeyer et al. ( 2011   ), 
6:208:16076:10:0:70:296:74:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:Benmelech (2012  ), and    Kearns and Patel    (2016  ).  
7:209:16136:0:18:102:528:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:The  analysis  also supports a  rapidly  growing  literature  that  shows  that even  when 
7:210:16227:18:19:75:528:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:macroprudential FX regulations work in terms of their direct goals, there can be leakages and 
7:211:16320:19:19:75:528:669:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:unintended consequences.7 Ranciere et al. (2010) highlight the importance of incorporating 
7:212:16411:19:19:75:528:650:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:these potential leakages in any analysis of the impact of macroprudential FX regulations. In 
7:213:16504:19:18:75:529:631:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:our analysis, these leakages are smaller than the direct effects of FX regulations, but still 
7:214:16598:18:31:75:280:613:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:significant and economically meaningful.  
7:215:16640:31:19:102:528:582:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A: Finally, this paper moves beyond most   other work     on macroprudential regulations by 
7:216:16730:19:19:75:528:563:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:assessing if the regulations  achieve the broader goal of improving financial resilience. The 
7:217:16824:19:18:75:528:544:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:results suggest that macroprudential FX  regulations can improve  the resilience of the banking 
7:218:16920:18:19:75:528:526:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:sector to currency fluctuations, but do less to improve the resilience of the broader economy 
7:219:17014:19:19:75:528:507:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:to currency fluctuations. This may still provide net benefits by improving the resilience of 
7:220:17107:19:19:75:528:488:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:banking institutions  that  can  create  broader  systemic  vulnerabilities,  just  as when  the 
7:221:17204:19:18:75:535:469:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:snowplow moves the snow off the road, it makes the road system safer. Yet , just as the snow 
7:222:17297:18:19:76:528:451:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:plow inevitably pushes a portion of the snow to block your driveway, macroprudential FX 
7:223:17385:19:19:76:528:432:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations can also shift some vulnerability to other sectors that are outside the regulatory 
7:224:17480:19:19:76:528:413:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:perimeter. These other institutions may be harder to monitor and less well informed than 
7:225:17569:19:18:76:529:394:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:banks, less able to screen for the risks inherent in corporate borrowing in FX, and less able to 
7:226:17666:18:19:76:541:376:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:handle subsequent losses after a depreciation. This shifting snowbank of r  isks could mitigate 
7:227:17762:19:31:76:370:357:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:some of the benefits  of the macroprudential FX regulations.  
7:228:17824:31:19:102:528:326:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:This paper proceeds as follows. Section II  presents the theoretical model of bank and 
7:229:17911:19:18:76:528:307:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:market lending in domestic and foreign currency. Section III  describes the data, including the 
7:230:18007:18:19:76:528:289:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:compilation  of  the dataset  on  macroprudential  FX  regulations. Section IV  presents the 
7:231:18100:19:19:76:528:270:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:empirical framework and reports results on the direct and indirect effects of FX regulations 
7:232:18193:19:19:75:540:251:116:g_d0_f2:116:g_d0_f2:F:on bank and firm borrowing and debt issuance  , including tests assessing the impact of different 
7:233:18291:19:18:75:528:232:116:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:measures and sensitivity tests. Section V assesses the impact of  the regulations on bank and 
7:234:18385:18:19:75:528:214:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:corporate  vulnerability  to  currency  movements,  including  how  this  corresponds  to other 
7:235:18481:19:31:75:338:195:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:measures of bank performance. Section VI concludes.

7:238:18587:8:13:70:537:107:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:7 Several papers documenting these leakages of regulations to other sectors are: Aiyar et al. (2014), Reinhardt and

8:242:19090:0:30:102:227:706:122:Georgia:122:Georgia:A:II. Theoretical Model 
8:243:19110:30:19:102:528:676:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Before assessing the impact of macroprudential FX regulations, we develop a simple 
8:244:19193:19:19:75:528:657:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:framework of bank versus market lending in domestic or foreign currency. This framework 
8:245:19281:19:19:75:528:638:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:shares with the seminal work of Holmstrom and Tirole (1997) the emphasis on asymmetric 
8:246:19368:19:18:75:528:619:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:information between lenders and borrowers, with banks as special lenders because of their 
8:247:19458:18:19:75:528:601:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:ability to reduce the consequences of asymmetric information at a cost. In Holmstrom and 
8:248:19547:19:19:75:528:582:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Tirole (1997), banks can monitor firms to reduce their moral hazard problem—a channel that 
8:249:19638:19:19:75:528:563:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:is absent in our model. Instead, we focus on how asymmetric information affects a lender’s 
8:250:19729:19:18:75:529:544:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:choice of the currency of their loans, where screening allows banks to identify more productive 
8:251:19825:18:19:75:528:526:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:firms that   are more likely to remain solvent after currency depreciations.8 While Holmstrom 
8:252:19919:19:19:75:529:507:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:and Tirole (1997) consider an environment with a single good, we  consider two goods in order 
8:253:20013:19:19:75:528:488:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:to   allow for a choice between foreign and    domestic currency.  Our model is not intended to 
8:254:20109:19:18:75:528:469:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:explain all of the factors that go into firm borrowing decisions, but instead provide structure 
8:255:20205:18:31:75:499:451:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:and a framework for the key channels evaluated in the empirical analysis in the paper.9 
8:256:20292:31:20:102:528:420:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:To begin, assume that   there are two dates, 푡푡= 0, 1, and a domestic D and a foreign F 
8:257:20378:20:19:75:528:400:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:good  .  Let 푒푒푡푡 be the exogenous exchange rate (the value of D goods in terms of F goods) at date 
8:258:20478:19:19:75:528:381:122:g_d0_f6:122:g_d0_f2:B:푡푡. We focus on FX risk (that is, the volatility of the exchange rate), with   no changes to its 
8:259:20575:19:19:75:528:362:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:expected level, which we normalize to one, 퐸퐸0 [푒푒1]=  푒푒0≡1. Specifically, the exchange rate 
8:260:20668:19:31:75:465:343:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:process is bivariate and can involve either depreciation or appreciation   :     
8:261:20749:31:32:156:464:312:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:    푒푒1 ∈ {푒푒퐿퐿,푒푒퐻퐻} ,        (1)  
8:262:20778:32:31:84:505:280:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:where 푒푒퐿퐿< 1 <  푒푒퐻퐻 and the probability of an appreciation is Pr{푒푒1=  푒푒퐻퐻} ≡푞푞 ∈ (0, 1). 
8:263:20868:31:19:102:535:249:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:The economy is populated by four    groups of risk-neutral agents: domestic firms, bank s, 
8:264:20959:19:18:75:528:230:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:investors, and savers. There are many banks,  investors, and    savers, each of whom take the 
8:265:21053:18:19:75:528:212:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:observable funding and lending rates as given and make zero profits due to competition.10 A 
8:266:21145:19:19:75:528:193:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:unit continuum of savers is  each    endowed with 퐾퐾퐷퐷 units of the domestic good and 퐾퐾퐹퐹 units of 
8:267:21245:19:20:75:526:174:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:the foreign good, respectively. The outside option of savers is given by constant-returns-to-
8:268:21338:20:19:75:528:154:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:scale technologies  that yield 푟푟퐷퐷 and 푟푟퐹퐹< 푟푟퐷퐷 at 푡푡= 1,    respectively. Thus, banks and investors 
8:269:21442:19:19:75:528:135:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:can  fund themselves in  domestic and foreign currency at these rates. Banks and investors are 
8:270:21537:19:8:228:231:116:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
8:271:21592:8:11:70:451:108:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:8 Stiglitz and Weiss (1981) is a seminal paper modelling bank screening in a one-good economy. 
8:272:21686:11:13:70:537:97:42:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:9 For example, the model and paper do not attempt to explain structural differences across countries in the reliance 
8:273:21802:13:8:70:260:84:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:on bank funding versus other forms of funding. 
8:274:21848:8:0:70:485:76:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:10 Our  results can be generalized to a setting in which lenders and firms share the surplus from lending.   
9:275:21958:0:31:75:410:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:hedged, so they obtain funding in the currency of the loan to firms.11  
9:276:22030:31:19:102:528:675:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:At 푡푡= 0, a unit continuum of firms 푗푗 ∈[0,1] has a domestic investment opportunity 
9:277:22113:19:18:75:565:656:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:normalized to unit size. Since firms do not have    their    own funds, they seek to borrow from 
9:278:22210:18:20:75:528:638:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:either banks or investors in either domestic or foreign currency. Firms are heterogeneous in 
9:279:22303:20:20:75:569:618:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:the  productivity of their opportunities, which yield a safe return 퐴퐴푗푗 at 푡푡= 1.   Firm    productivity 
9:280:22408:20:31:75:501:598:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:is private information,  but   the   distribution is publicly known and    can take three values:

14:461:34415:31:31:120:459:343:122:g_d0_f2:122:Georgia:C: iii. Evaluating the impact of macroprudential FX regulation

15:489:36177:31:19:84:528:400:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:In contrast, after macroprudential FX regulation, no bank lends in F and no bank fails after 
15:490:36270:19:19:84:528:381:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:a depreciation of the domestic currency. The realized bank profit from lending in 퐹퐹 after 
15:491:36361:19:19:84:528:362:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:regulation  is  zero  for  both  realized  exchange  rates  and  completely  insensitive  to  the

15:494:36650:19:19:84:528:306:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:FX risk. The exposure of firms that still receive FX funding is unchanged, but some firms no 
15:495:36743:19:19:84:528:287:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:longer receive FX funding. As a result, the net effect is  only a small reduction in firm 
15:496:36833:19:30:84:484:268:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:sensitivity to currency movements (and less of a reduction than occurs for banks). 
15:497:36915:30:31:102:318:238:122:Georgia:122:Georgia:A:D. Testable implications of the model 
15:498:36951:31:19:102:528:207:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:This section has developed a stylized model of informed bank and uninformed market 
15:499:37034:19:19:75:528:188:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:lending in domestic and foreign currency. This model yields four testable implications about 
15:500:37127:19:30:75:341:169:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:the effects of FX macroprudential regulation of banks: 
15:501:37181:30:19:102:528:139:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:(1) Banks borrow and lend less in foreign currency (but do not change their borrowing 
15:502:37266:19:14:75:187:120:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:in  domestic currency). 
15:503:37289:14:0:102:103:106:36:g_d0_f2:36:g_d0_f2:A: 
16:504:37292:0:18:102:547:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:(2) Some firms    shift away from banks to incre   ase their FX borrowing from market 
16:505:37377:18:14:75:417:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:investors (with no increase in non-FX borrowing by firms and banks). 
16:506:37445:14:15:102:103:674:36:g_d0_f2:36:g_d0_f2:A: 
16:507:37445:15:14:102:451:659:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:(3) Bank s’ expos   ure   to exchange rate movements declines significantly. 
16:508:37521:14:15:102:103:645:36:g_d0_f2:36:g_d0_f2:A: 
16:509:37521:15:19:102:529:630:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:(4) Firms' exposure to exchange rate movements declines moderately, and by less than 
16:510:37605:19:19:75:149:611:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:that for banks. 
16:511:37620:19:19:102:105:592:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A: 
16:512:37620:19:30:102:283:573:122:Georgia:122:Georgia:A:E. An extension with exporters 
16:513:37649:30:19:102:528:543:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:In an effort to keep the model parsimonious and focus on the key channels that are the 
16:514:37736:19:19:84:529:524:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:focus of the empirical analysis, we do not explicitly differentiate between smaller, more 
16:515:37826:19:19:84:528:505:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:domestically-focused firms and larger, export-oriented firms. This differentiation could be 
16:516:37918:19:18:84:528:486:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:important, however, if  exporting firms have a natural hedge against currency movements 
16:517:38006:18:19:84:528:468:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:and    are  therefore be more likely to obtain cheap funding in foreign currency, irrespective of 
16:518:38104:19:19:84:528:449:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:whether macroprudential FX regulations are in place.16 Therefore, we have also developed 
16:519:38193:19:31:84:334:430:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:a version of the model to incorporate this scenario. 
16:520:38245:31:18:102:528:399:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:More specifically, evidence suggests that exporters  tend to be larger and more productive 
16:521:38335:18:19:84:539:381:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:than non-exporters (e.g., Bernard et al., 20  03,   Melitz, 2003), so   we extend our framework 
16:522:38431:19:20:84:536:362:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:to assume that some high-productive firms are exporters. A   fraction of their output 퐴퐴퐻퐻 is  a 
16:523:38528:20:19:84:528:342:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:good   that is priced in 퐹퐹, offering a natural hedge against FX risk. The status of exporters is 
16:524:38626:19:19:84:528:323:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:publicly observable, so    investors can  infer    that these firms have high  productivity. Hence, 
16:525:38726:19:19:84:528:304:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:the competitive lending rate is 휌휌퐸퐸∗=푟푟퐹퐹 . This    cost of market funding in 퐹퐹 to exporters is 
16:526:38824:19:19:84:528:285:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:cheaper than bank funding in either currency, so exporters prefer to obtain funding from 
16:527:38913:19:31:84:387:266:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:investors in 퐹퐹–irrespective of macroprudential FX regulation. 
16:528:38975:31:19:102:528:235:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:All of the key implications from the model developed above continue to hold, except that 
16:529:39063:19:18:84:528:216:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:now   exporters default less often after a depreciation of the domestic currency. This lower 
16:530:39156:18:19:84:528:198:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:default probability is partly due to their natural hedge (with a share of production priced in 
16:531:39251:19:22:84:534:179:122:g_d0_f5:122:g_d0_f2:A:F), and partly due to their  cheaper funding.   Specifically, for  an intermediate depreciation 
16:532:39347:22:7:84:236:157:122:g_d0_f6:65:g_d0_f6:A:푒푒퐿퐿∈[푒푒퐿퐿,푒푒퐿퐿�], where 푒푒퐿퐿≡푟푟퐹퐹−휙휙퐴퐴퐻퐻(1−휙휙)퐴퐴
16:533:39396:7:0:236:241:150:42:g_d0_f6:42:g_d0_f6:?:퐻퐻
16:534:39398:0:25:242:529:157:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:, an   exporting firm does not default after having received 
16:535:39459:25:36:84:480:132:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:market funding in 퐹퐹,  but would have defaulted after receiving bank funding in 퐹퐹.  
16:536:39544:36:9:228:231:96:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
16:537:39599:9:13:70:537:87:42:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:16 For example, Kalemli-Ozcan et al.   (2016) show that exporters have a higher share of dollar debt than non-exporters 
16:538:39717:13:0:70:170:74:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:in  Latin American firms. 
17:539:39745:0:30:102:213:706:122:Georgia:122:Georgia:A:III. The Data  
17:540:39758:30:19:102:528:676:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:This section discusses the data used for the empirical analysis. It is divided into two 
17:541:39846:19:19:75:533:657:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:parts.  The  first  provides  details  on  the  newly  compiled  dataset  on  macroprudential  FX 
17:542:39944:19:19:75:528:638:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations that is central to this paper. The second discusses the additional explanatory and 
17:543:40039:19:30:75:263:619:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:control variables used in the  analysis.  
17:544:40081:30:31:102:356:589:122:Georgia:122:g_d0_f2:A:A. Data on Macroprudential FX Regulations 
17:545:40121:31:19:102:528:558:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:We define macroprudential FX regulations as regulations that discriminate based on the 
17:546:40208:19:19:75:528:539:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:currency denomination of a capital transaction.17 Macroprudential FX regulations usually 
17:547:40297:19:18:75:528:520:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:focus on the domestic banking system and can be implemented by the government, the central 
17:548:40388:18:19:75:528:502:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:bank, or the national prudential regulator. Our measures of macroprudential FX regulations 
17:549:40479:19:19:75:528:483:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:do not include capital controls—which discriminate by the residency of the parties involved in 
17:550:40574:19:19:75:528:464:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:the transaction—although there is substantial overlap in these two types of measures given 
17:551:40665:19:18:75:528:445:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:that   transactions between residents and non-residents are more likely to involve FX. Also, 
17:552:40758:18:19:75:528:427:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:while our measures are  macroprudential, as they are directed at systemic risks to the entire 
17:553:40852:19:19:75:528:408:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:financial system stemming from FX flows and exposures, some measures (such as sectoral FX 
17:554:40942:19:19:75:528:389:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:capital risk weights) can also be classified as microprudential regulations (which generally 
17:555:41035:19:30:75:351:370:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:target the resilience of individual financial institutions).  
17:556:41096:30:19:102:528:340:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:To construct our database, we draw on four sources on   macro-prudential regulations: 
17:557:41182:19:19:75:528:321:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Shim et al. (2013  ), Vandenbussche et al. (2015), Cerutti et al. (2017), and Reinhardt and 
17:558:41273:19:19:75:525:302:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Sowerbutts (2018). Each of these datasets uses different sources and has a different focus—
17:559:41364:19:18:75:528:283:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f5:B:but includes some information on macroprudential FX regulations. More specifically, Shim et 
17:560:41456:18:19:75:533:265:122:g_d0_f5:122:g_d0_f2:B:al. (2013  ) provides  verbal descriptions of policy events broadly related to the housing sector 
17:561:41554:19:19:75:545:246:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:for  60  countries  at  a  monthly  frequency from 1990 -2012. Vandenbussche et  al.  (2015  ) 
17:562:41649:19:19:75:541:227:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:provides  detailed data on   a broad range of macroprudential policy actions for 16 countries 
17:563:41743:19:18:75:528:208:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:from Emerging Europe over the period 1997-2010. Cerutti et al. (2017) uses an IMF database 
17:564:41834:18:19:75:532:190:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:on country surveys to provide measures for 12 macroprudential policies, including on FX-  and 
17:565:41928:19:19:75:528:171:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:local-   currency reserve requirements, in a set of 64 countries over 2000-14. Finally, Reinhardt 
17:566:42026:19:19:75:528:152:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:and Sowerbutts (2018) build a database on macroprudential policy actions for 60 countries 
17:567:42116:19:49:75:556:133:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:starting in 1995. For   more details  on the construction  of this    dataset on macroprudential FX 
17:568:42216:49:8:228:231:84:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
17:569:42271:8:0:70:523:76:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:17 Throughout the paper, we use the terms “macroprudential FX regulations” and “FX regulations” synonymously. 
18:570:42383:0:30:75:327:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations, see Appendix A in Ahnert et al. (2018). 
18:571:42436:30:19:102:528:676:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:After combining these sources, our dataset includes information on 132 changes in 
18:572:42518:19:19:75:528:657:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:macroprudential FX regulations from 1995 through 2014 (on a quarterly basis) that represent 
18:573:42610:19:19:75:528:638:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:either a tightening or loosening in regulation. This full sample includes both advanced and 
18:574:42702:19:18:75:537:619:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:emerging economies, but we exclude reserve-issuing countries (i.e., long -standing members 
18:575:42793:18:19:75:528:601:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:of the Euro Area, the US, Switzerland and Japan) to focus on countries more vulnerable to 
18:576:42883:19:19:75:528:582:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:currency mismatches and the global financial cycle. We also exclude offshore centers, as 
18:577:42972:19:19:75:528:563:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:defined by the BIS in International Banking Statistics, with the exception of Singapore and 
18:578:43064:19:18:75:528:544:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Hong Kong. This leaves us with a sample of 48 countries for our main empirical analysis.18 
18:579:43154:18:19:75:528:526:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Some countries have made no changes to macroprudential FX policy, while others have made 
18:580:43243:19:19:75:528:507:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:more than ten . There is good coverage of countries in Asia, Europe, and South America, but 
18:581:43335:19:31:75:357:488:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:coverage is more limited for   the Middle East and Africa.19 
18:582:43395:31:18:102:540:457:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 1  shows the cumulated changes in all macroprudential FX regulations from 1995   
18:583:43483:18:19:75:529:439:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:through 2015. Any adoption or tightening of each regulation in the dataset is counted as a +1, 
18:584:43578:19:19:75:528:420:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:and any reduction or removal is a -1, with the graph showing the cumulated total on the given 
18:585:43672:19:19:75:528:401:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:date.   The figure shows a general trend of  tightening FX regulations since the mid-2000s, 
18:586:43764:19:18:75:528:382:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:interrupted by a brief period of loosening during the Global Financial Crisis. In our dataset, 
18:587:43859:18:19:75:528:364:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:these macroprudential FX regulations can be further disaggregated into those focusing on 
18:588:43948:19:32:75:422:345:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:banks’ FX assets and those on banks’ FX liabilities.20 More specifically: 
18:589:44021:32:19:84:528:313:122:g_d0_f10:122:g_d0_f2:A:• FX  Asset-side  Measures  (in blue) include all policies aimed at the FX assets of 
18:590:44104:19:18:102:528:294:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:domestic  banks.  These  generally  focus  on  restricting  FX  lending  to  corporates  and 
18:591:44197:18:19:102:528:276:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:households in the domestic economy. These measures include FX capital regulations for 
18:592:44283:19:19:102:528:257:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:banks (such as provisioning rules or risk weights associated with FX-lending). These also 
18:593:44373:19:19:102:528:238:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:include  l ending  standards  for  FX  loans,  incorporating  both quantitative  lending 
18:594:44462:19:18:102:528:219:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:standards ( such as loan-to-value (LTV) ratios or debt-to-income (DTI) ratios for FX 
18:595:44547:18:19:102:537:201:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:loans ),  and  qualitative  lending  standards  for  FX  loans  ( such  as  amortization 
18:596:44636:19:36:102:242:182:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:requirements for FX loans).  
18:597:44663:36:8:228:231:146:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
18:598:44718:8:13:71:537:138:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:F:18 The full list of countries is reported in Table A1 in Ahnert et al. (2018), with the cumulated number of changes in 
18:599:44837:13:8:71:279:125:81:g_d0_f2:99:g_d0_f2:F:each type of macroprudential regulation by country. 
18:600:44888:8:12:70:537:117:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f5:?:19 Our sample includes 17 advanced economies and 31 emerging markets (as classified by the BIS in their International 
18:601:45006:12:11:70:537:105:81:g_d0_f5:81:g_d0_f2:?:Banking Statistics). Advanced economies increased their use of FX regulations towards the end of the sample, but 
18:602:45119:11:7:70:360:94:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:emerging markets account for the vast majority of FX regulatory actions. 
18:603:45191:7:13:70:537:87:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:20 These two categories can be further disaggregated into various subcategories. We do not focus on the more detailed 
18:604:45309:13:0:70:482:74:81:g_d0_f2:99:g_d0_f2:?:disaggregation in this paper, however, as the sample size becomes too small to yield meaningful results. 
19:605:45416:0:18:84:528:705:122:g_d0_f10:122:g_d0_f2:A:• FX Liability-side Measures (in red) include all policies aimed at the FX liabilities of 
19:606:45505:18:19:102:528:687:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:domestic banks. These measures generally focus on the funding decisions of banks and 
19:607:45590:19:19:102:528:668:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:include FX  reserve  requirements  and  FX  liquidity  requirements (such  as  liquidity 
19:608:45679:19:19:102:529:649:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:coverage ratios or taxes on non-core FX liabilities). These measures tend to specifically 
19:609:45769:19:30:102:288:630:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:target FX flows with a short maturity. 
19:610:45807:30:19:102:504:600:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:The shaded areas in Figure 1  show     the cumulated actions for these two types of FX 
19:611:45894:19:19:84:515:581:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:measures,  with    30 cumulated liability-side regulations and 37  cumulated asset   -s ide 
19:612:45986:19:19:84:521:562:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:measures at  the end of the sample period. Asset-side FX regulations started to be adopted 
19:613:46077:19:18:84:507:543:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:more rapidly just before the global financial crisis, and then experienced another surge 
19:614:46166:18:19:84:529:525:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:around 2010-11, but have since been adopted at a more moderate pace. Liability  -side FX 
19:615:46255:19:19:85:513:506:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:regulations were adopted more gradually from 2002-2006, after which use fell by about 
19:616:46341:19:19:85:514:487:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:half,    until    after 2010 they regained attention and their use roughly doubled during 2010-
19:617:46436:19:18:85:524:468:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:13.  These different types of macroprudential FX regulations could have different effects on 
19:618:46529:18:19:85:516:450:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:the economy. For example, measures targeting banks’ FX liabilities might affect their FX 
19:619:46618:19:19:85:521:431:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:lending to all their borrowers, while asset-side measures might only restrict FX lending to 
19:620:46710:19:31:85:392:412:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:specific borrowers (for example those lacking a natural hedge). 
19:621:46773:31:18:103:535:381:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:For a final cut of the data, Figure 2  uses the same categories to break out the number of 
19:622:46864:18:19:76:529:363:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:times each macroprudential FX measure was either tightened or loosened. This is useful to 
19:623:46954:19:19:76:528:344:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:better understand what is driving the cumulated statistics in Figure 1, as “no change” in the 
19:624:47048:19:19:76:529:325:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:cumulated graphs could mask no change in the given regulation by any country, or a number 
19:625:47138:19:18:76:528:306:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:of countries which tightened the measure while an equal number simultaneously loosened. 
19:626:47226:18:19:76:528:288:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Figure 2  shows that, in many periods, the latter is the case—with some years when a large 
19:627:47317:19:19:76:534:269:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:number of countries simultaneously tightened and loosened different policies. Figure 2  also 
19:628:47410:19:19:75:528:250:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:provides  more  detail  on  the phases of  tightening and  loosening in  macroprudential  FX 
19:629:47503:19:30:75:227:231:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations shown in Figure 1.  
19:630:47535:30:31:102:447:201:122:Georgia:122:g_d0_f2:A:B. Data on International Capital Flows and other Variables   
19:631:47595:31:19:102:528:170:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:This section begins by discussing the international capital flow variables on bank and 
19:632:47682:19:19:75:528:151:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:corporate borrowing that will be the focus of the empirical tests. It closes with a discussion of 
19:633:47780:19:30:75:222:132:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:the  various control variables.  
19:634:47812:30:19:102:525:102:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:To begin, in order to test model prediction #1 on the impact of FX  regulations on cross-
19:635:47901:19:0:75:528:83:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:border loans to banks, we use quarterly data from the BIS International Banking Statistics 
20:636:47995:0:18:75:528:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:(IBS)   , which reports both FX and non-FX gross capital inflows to banks. These data are 
20:637:48085:18:19:75:528:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:expressed as a percent of annual GDP ( calculated as 4-quarter moving averages).21 In order to 
20:638:48180:19:19:75:529:669:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:test model prediction #2 on the spillover effects of the regulations, we use data from the BIS 
20:639:48275:19:19:75:533:650:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:International  Debt  Statistics  (IDS),  which  includes  debt  securities  issued  by  domestic 
20:640:48372:19:30:75:441:631:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:headquartered companies on international markets in FX and non-FX.    
20:641:48442:30:19:102:563:601:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 3  graph   s  several of these measures which will be a focus of the empirical analysis. 
20:642:48538:19:19:75:528:582:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Figure 3a shows the evolution of cross-border loans to banks as a percent of GDP, broken into 
20:643:48632:19:19:75:528:563:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:loans in FX (red) and non-FX (blue). This shows the decline in cross-border lending since 
20:644:48722:19:18:75:528:544:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:around the crisis, with basically all of the decline occurring in FX lending. Figure 3b shows 
20:645:48816:18:19:75:528:526:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:international debt issuance over the same period, also broken down into FX (solid lines) and 
20:646:48909:19:19:75:547:507:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:non-   FX borrowing (dashed lines), and further distinguished into borrowing by banks (green) 
20:647:49003:19:19:75:528:488:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:and corporates (orange). This shows that international debt issuance in FX has increased 
20:648:49092:19:18:75:528:469:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:fairly  steadily since the crisis for corporates, but fallen for banks. Non-FX borrowing by 
20:649:49184:18:19:75:528:451:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:corporates has been fairly flat, and for banks has decreased. These graphs are only suggestive, 
20:650:49280:19:19:75:528:432:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:but the trends agree with the model’s prediction; after a tightening in macroprudential FX 
20:651:49371:19:19:75:528:413:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations (such as after the 2008 crisis), cross-border FX lending by banks declines (with 
20:652:49464:19:18:75:528:394:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:no change in non-FX lending by banks), while corporate debt issuance in FX increases (with 
20:653:49555:18:31:75:525:376:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:no increase in corporate non-FX debt issuance or bank debt issuance in FX or non-FX).     
20:654:49645:31:19:102:528:345:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:The empirical analysis also includes a number of control variables that merit discussion. 
20:655:49735:19:19:75:528:326:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:These variables were chosen to be consistent with existing literature, most closely following 
20:656:49829:19:18:75:529:307:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:recent work on the determinants of cross-border bank flows in Avdjiev et al. (2016a) and 
20:657:49918:18:19:75:532:289:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Bruno and Shin (2016).  An innovation in our control variables is that when we calculate the 
20:658:50011:19:19:75:528:270:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:exposure of country i to certain variables in other countries, we weight the respective variable 
20:659:50108:19:19:75:528:251:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:by  country i’s  “financial  exposure”  instead  of  its  trade  exposure.  As shown  in  Lane  and 
20:660:50208:19:18:75:528:232:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Shambaugh (2010) and Bénétrix et al. (2015), this can be important when countries have 
20:661:50295:18:19:76:529:214:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:different currency than trade exposures (such as many emerging markets which are more 
20:662:50381:19:19:76:528:195:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:exposed to US dollar movements than predicted based purely on trade patterns). A sensitivity 
20:663:50474:19:31:76:381:176:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:test shows that this weighting does not impact the key results.  
20:664:50538:31:18:103:549:145:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:We include five variables in our baseline specification, focusing on variables with    some 
20:665:50630:18:32:76:522:127:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:time   variation so that they are   not   absorbed in the   country fixed effects. These controls are:  
20:666:50733:32:8:228:231:95:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:

20:668:50908:13:0:70:479:74:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:therefore they should not be affected by exchange-rate valuation effects. See Appendix A  of this paper.  
21:669:51017:0:18:102:528:705:122:g_d0_f10:122:g_d0_f2:A:• Changes  in  non-FX  macroprudential  regulation:  measured  by  calculating  any

21:672:51298:19:19:75:528:649:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:for country i. Then any changes in FX regulations are removed. The resulting measure is

21:687:52620:18:19:75:528:309:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:YEN,  CHF).  This  controls  for  the  return/funding  costs  of  FX  loans  relative  to  the

21:689:52804:19:32:75:376:271:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:funding differentials for the most relevant countries/regions.

23:744:57533:19:18:75:528:427:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:the FX share of total net debt issuance by each group. (Extensions also consider the impact of 
23:745:57628:18:31:75:435:409:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations on total loans to banks and total debt issuance by corporates.)

23:752:58256:31:20:102:528:253:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:A final important point in equation (16)    is the time fixed effects (δt), which are included

23:756:58630:19:19:75:528:177:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:factors are most important (such as the role of global risk or monetary policy in advanced 
23:757:58721:19:33:75:528:158:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:economies). By controlling for a global-time fixed effect, we do not need to take a stance on 
23:758:58815:33:8:228:231:125:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
23:759:58870:8:12:70:537:117:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:24 To ensure that large observations are not driving the results, all dependent and independent variables are winsorised 
23:760:58991:12:11:70:536:105:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:at the 2.5% level (except for variables based on bounded indices). In order to account for exchange rate valuation 
23:761:59106:11:10:70:537:94:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:effects, changes in shares are calculated based on a series of stocks calculated by adding cumulated exchange rate 
23:762:59221:10:10:70:536:84:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:adjusted changes in bank loans and deposits or net issuance of debt securities to initial stocks. Before winsorising the 
23:763:59342:10:0:70:378:74:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:resulting shares, we exclude changes in shares above +100% or below -100%. 
24:764:59420:0:18:75:528:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:exactly which global factors are important, or worry about time effects shared by all countries 
24:765:59516:18:19:75:528:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:that are difficult to measure. To show that this assumption does not affect our main results,

24:769:59892:18:31:75:498:613:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:different specifications of global factors have no meaningful impact on the key results.

28:915:73217:19:19:75:528:389:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:side of bank balance sheets (i.e., aimed at raising the cost of FX funding of domestic banks) 
28:916:73311:19:18:75:528:370:122:g_d0_f2:116:g_d0_f2:B:work through somewhat different channels than those targeting the asset-side (i.e., aimed at 
28:917:73404:18:19:75:528:352:116:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:raising the cost of bank FX lending to households and corporates in the domestic economy). This 
28:918:73500:19:19:75:528:333:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:section  tests for  any  differential  effects  of  the  various  forms  of  macroprudential  FX 
28:919:73597:19:19:75:528:314:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations.  These results should be interpreted cautiously, however, as these finer divisions 
28:920:73693:19:18:75:528:295:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:of  different  forms  of macroprudential  FX  regulations  imply  that  there  are  more  limited 
28:921:73791:18:31:75:250:277:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:degrees of freedom for the analysis. 
28:922:73828:31:19:102:533:246:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:To begin, we  focus on any differential effects if the FX macroprudential regulations 
28:923:73914:19:19:75:528:227:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:target banks’ assets or liabilities, using the definitions discussed in Section III.A.31 Results are 
28:924:74015:19:18:75:528:208:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:shown in Table 3, which repeats the baseline framework from Tables 1 and 2, with the full set 
28:925:74109:18:19:75:543:190:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:of control variables and global-period dummy variables.32 The results are similar for   asset- 
28:926:74204:19:19:75:528:171:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:and liability-based measures when assessing the effect on cross-border loans to banks, but 
28:927:74295:19:18:75:542:152:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:differ when assessing the impact on FX   debt issuance by corporates. More specifically, both 
28:928:74389:18:28:75:528:134:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:asset- and  liability-side  FX  measures  are  correlated  with  a  significant  decrease  in  FX 
28:929:74487:28:9:228:231:106:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
28:930:74542:9:13:70:537:97:42:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:31 We h   ave also examined effects using narrower definitions of FX regulations, but the number of regulatory actions 
28:931:74659:13:8:70:520:84:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:quickly becomes so limited that results become sensitive to minor changes in specification and country inclusion. 
28:932:74772:8:0:70:534:76:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:32 Results are basically identical when the individual global variables are included instead of the global-time dummy. 
29:933:74894:0:18:75:526:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:borrowing by banks—with the magnitude of the coefficient estimated to be larger for asset-
29:934:74984:18:19:75:531:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:side regulations,  but only significant at the 10% level in column (8). For both measures, FX 
29:935:75078:19:19:75:528:669:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations continue to have a positive effect on FX debt issuance by corporates—but this 
29:936:75168:19:19:75:528:650:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:effect is only estimated to be significant (at either the 5% or 10% level) for liability-side 
29:937:75262:19:18:75:528:631:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations. The magnitude of the coefficient on FX debt issuance is also estimated to be about 
29:938:75358:18:19:75:528:613:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:three times large   r  for liability-  side than asset-side regulations (In both cases, there continues 
29:939:75462:19:31:75:457:594:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:to  be no significant effect on non-FX debt issuance by corporates and banks.).  
29:940:75543:31:19:102:532:563:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:These results suggest that both asset- and liability-side FX measures are effective in  their 
29:941:75637:19:18:76:528:544:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:direct goal of reducing cross-border loans to banks in FX. Only the liability-side measures, 
29:942:75730:18:19:76:542:526:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:however,  may  also  have  the  unintended side  -effect  of  increasing FX    debt  issuance  by 
29:943:75828:19:19:76:531:507:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:corporates.  Repeating  the calculations  to  gauge  the  degree  of “shifting”,  an  increase  in 
29:944:75927:19:19:76:537:488:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:lia bility   -side   FX  measures causes FX debt issuance by corporates to increase by 16%  of the 
29:945:76026:19:18:76:528:469:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:reduction in FX loans  by banks (instead of 10% when all FX regulations are aggregated).33 In 
29:946:76120:18:19:75:557:451:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:other words, liability-side regulations appear to cause more    “shifting snowbanks”    of  currency 
29:947:76221:19:19:75:528:432:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:vulnerability  from  banks  to  other  sectors.  As  a  result,  asset-side  regulations  may better 
29:948:76322:19:19:75:528:413:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:improve a country’s  resilience to currency movements, as they decrease bank exposure to 
29:949:76411:19:30:75:480:394:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:currency risk but simultaneously generate less shifting of this risk to other sectors.  
29:950:76498:30:19:102:528:364:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:One possible reason for these differential effects, as suggested in the theoretical model, 
29:951:76589:19:19:75:528:345:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:is that liability-based measures affect all forms of bank funding in all states of the world. In 
29:952:76686:19:19:75:528:326:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:contrast, asset-based measures only affect bank lending, and often only certain segments of 
29:953:76778:19:18:75:528:307:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:bank lending (such as through mortgages) —   thus    affecting a smaller share of bank balance 
29:954:76873:18:19:75:528:289:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:sheets and having a smaller aggregate effect. Closely related, if  asset-   side regulations primarily 
29:955:76976:19:19:75:528:270:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:affect  bank  lending  to  households,  while  liability-side  regulations  affect  lending  to  both 
29:956:77078:19:19:75:528:251:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:corporates and households, it is  natural that tighter liability-side FX regulations correspond 
29:957:77174:19:18:75:528:232:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:to  a greater response in the corporate sector. Supporting this hypothesis, in some countries 
29:958:77268:18:19:75:528:214:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:most    FX regulations target the asset-   side  , a large share of which are regulations on LTV ratios, 
29:959:77373:19:19:75:529:195:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:DTI ratios, and other aspects of FX lending for mortgages (such as in Hungary and Poland). 
29:960:77464:19:19:75:538:176:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:A  final    possible explanation is  the maturity of the capital flows targeted by the se different 
29:961:77564:19:18:75:526:157:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:measures. FX liability-based measures tend to focus on shorter-term inflows, while FX asset-
29:962:77656:18:34:75:528:139:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:based measures tend to focus on longer-term maturities. As macroprudential measures often 
29:963:77746:34:8:228:231:105:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
29:964:77801:8:13:70:541:97:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:33 This is calculated as 0.0788 (Table 3, column 4) divided by 0.487 (Table 3, column 1). If one also incorporates that 
29:965:77921:13:10:70:541:84:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:only about 62% of FX loans from banks to non-banks are likely lent to the corporate sector, the degree of shifting 
29:966:78036:10:0:70:141:74:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:increases  to 26%. 
30:967:78058:0:18:75:526:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:involve a greater relative cost for short-term than longer-term capital flows, these shorter-
30:968:78151:18:31:75:262:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:term flows are the ones most affected. 
30:969:78189:31:19:102:528:657:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Macroprudential FX regulations could have different effects based not only on whether 
30:970:78275:19:19:75:531:638:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:they target assets or liabilities, but also based on how large the change in the regulation is . 
30:971:78372:19:18:75:528:619:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Assessing the intensity of changes in macroprudential regulation is difficult, however, because 
30:972:78468:18:19:75:528:601:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:most data on macroprudential regulations only records whether the regulation is tightened or 
30:973:78561:19:19:75:531:582:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:loosened using dummy variables (as in our data set). This is  the standard treatment in the 
30:974:78653:19:19:75:531:563:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:literature,  because  it  is  impossible  to  compare  discrete  changes  in  different  types  of 
30:975:78752:19:18:75:545:544:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations (i.e.,   a 10% increase in FX reserve requirements is unlikely to correspond to a 10% 
30:976:78850:18:19:75:528:526:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:increase in the FX  liquidity coverage ratio). It is even difficult to compare changes of the same 
30:977:78949:19:19:75:528:507:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:magnitude in  a  specific  FX  regulation  across  countries, given  different definitions and 
30:978:79044:19:19:75:528:488:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:coverage (i.e., a 10% increase in the liquidity coverage ratio can mean very different things 
30:979:79138:19:18:75:528:469:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:based on the country’s definition of what qualifies as a liquid asset). A few papers have shown 
30:980:79234:18:19:75:528:451:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:that    having more macroprudential  measures  in  place or   “major”  changes  in regulations 
30:981:79329:19:19:75:528:432:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:generate larger effects, results t hat   are   intuitive but do not provide concrete information on 
30:982:79429:19:31:75:505:413:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:how a given change in a regulation would be expected to affect a key outcome variable.34 
30:983:79517:31:18:102:528:382:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:In an effort to move beyond this standard treatment of macroprudential regulations, we 
30:984:79604:18:19:75:528:364:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:extend  our  analysis  to  estimate  the  impact  of  concrete  changes  in  specific regulatory 
30:985:79701:19:19:75:528:345:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:instruments. More specifically, we focus on two databases which provide information on the 
30:986:79792:19:19:75:528:326:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:intensity of macroprudential FX policies, albeit in a limited sample or for a limited set of 
30:987:79884:19:18:75:528:307:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:measures. First, Cerutti et al. (2017) includes data with information on the intensity of FX 
30:988:79977:18:19:75:528:289:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f5:B:reserve requirement changes for a sample similar to ours.35 Second, Vandenbussche et al. 
30:989:80066:19:19:75:532:270:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:(2012) includes information on the intensity of other types of regulations:  foreign currency 
30:990:80160:19:19:75:528:251:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:liquidity  requirements,  the   maximum ratio  of  foreign  currency  loans  to  own  funds,  risk 
30:991:80259:19:18:75:528:232:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:weights on foreign currency mortgage loans, consumer loans and corporate loans.  These more 
30:992:80351:18:19:75:529:214:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:detailed data, however, have    two    important disadvantages: the data ends in 2010 (thereby 
30:993:80446:19:19:75:550:195:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:missing a  period  of  active  use  of  macropr udential  FX  regulations)  and    the  data  is  only 
30:994:80549:19:38:75:436:176:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:available for Eastern Europe (thereby severely limiting country coverage). 
30:995:80624:38:9:228:231:138:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
30:996:80679:9:13:70:540:129:42:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:34 More specifically, Cerutti et al. (2017) c reate a measure which is the sum of the number of different types of 
30:997:80793:13:10:70:537:116:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:macroprudential measures in use. Forbes et al. (2015) classify a subset of their measures of capital controls and 
30:998:80907:10:10:70:537:106:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:macroprudential measures as those which were “major”, based on the attention by investors, financial analysts, or 
30:999:81021:10:9:70:490:96:81:g_d0_f2:99:g_d0_f2:?:international financial institutions (as assessed by coverage in analyst reports, IMF papers, and surveys).  
30:1000:81129:9:13:71:537:87:42:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:F:35 Specifically, the authors state that given the mostly quantitative nature of reserve requirements, values above or 
30:1001:81247:13:0:71:506:74:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:F:below 1 and –1 for their index can capture the intensity in the changes (with the index   ranging from    -3 to +5). 
31:1002:81367:0:18:102:528:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Keeping these    caveats in mind,  the   resulting estimates give some idea of the magnitude 
31:1003:81459:18:19:75:528:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:of the effects from these specif   ic FX regulations. First, a large increase in reserve requirements 
31:1004:81561:19:19:75:528:669:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:on foreign currency borrowing (proxied by the quantitative index taking a value of 5) leads to 
31:1005:81655:19:19:75:550:650:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:a decline in FX loans to banks by 0.46%    of GDP and an increase in FX international debt 
31:1006:81746:19:18:75:528:631:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:issuance by 0.15%  of GDP. Second, an increase in the foreign currency liquidity requirement 
31:1007:81839:18:19:75:528:613:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:by 10pp reduces FX loans to banks  by 2.9% of GDP and increases international FX debt 
31:1008:81925:19:19:75:528:594:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:issuance by corporates by 0.36% of GDP. Third   , a tightening in the maximum ratio of FX loans 
31:1009:82021:19:19:75:528:575:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:to own funds from 400% to 200% reduces FX loans to banks by around 1% of GDP and 
31:1010:82102:19:18:75:528:556:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:increases FX debt issuance by corporates by 0.05% of GDP.  Finally, an increase in the risk 
31:1011:82194:18:19:75:528:538:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:weight on foreign currency mortgage loans,  consumer loans or corporate loans by 50pp above 
31:1012:82286:19:19:75:528:519:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:the local currency risk weights reduces FX inflows to banks by 0.26%,   0.4 6%   or 1.83% of GDP, 
31:1013:82384:19:19:75:528:500:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:respectively, and corresponds to an increase in FX international debt issuance by corporates 
31:1014:82477:19:18:75:528:481:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:by about 0.07% of GDP in  each   case.    All of these estimated effects of specific changes in FX 
31:1015:82576:18:19:75:528:463:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations have the expected sign, and several of the estimates (such as for foreign currency 
31:1016:82671:19:31:75:488:444:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:liquidity requirements) are  consistently significant despite the limited sample size.36  
31:1017:82761:31:31:102:354:413:122:Georgia:122:Georgia:A:D. Endogeneity and Other Sensitivity Tests 
31:1018:82803:31:18:102:534:382:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:The   finding that macroprudential FX  regulations significantly reduce bank borrowing in 
31:1019:82893:18:19:75:528:364:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:FX and increase corporate debt issuance in FX are central to understanding the impact of 
31:1020:82982:19:19:75:544:345:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:these   regulations, so   we next perform a  series of robustness checks, including   specifications 
31:1021:83083:19:19:75:528:326:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:that should better identify the exogenous component of macroprudential regulations. For 
31:1022:83171:19:18:75:528:307:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:each test, we focus on whether macroprudential FX regulations decrease international bank 
31:1023:83261:18:19:75:529:289:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:borrowing (or share of borrowing) in FX and non-FX, and whether they increase corporate 
31:1024:83349:19:19:75:528:270:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:debt issuance (or share of debt issuance) in FX and non-FX (Tables 1 and 2, respectively). We 
31:1025:83443:19:19:75:528:251:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:do not report all of the “non-results” that are not significant (nor expected to be significant), 
31:1026:83541:19:30:75:413:232:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:as they continue to be insignificant in all of the tests discussed below. 
31:1027:83615:30:19:93:528:202:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:One potential concern with the baseline analysis is that   trends in our dependent variables 
31:1028:83708:19:19:75:528:183:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:could be driving changes in macroprudential policy instead of vice-versa (i.e., endogeneity).37 
31:1029:83803:19:18:75:529:164:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:For example, increased corporate debt issuance in FX could heighten concerns about risks to 
31:1030:83895:18:21:75:528:146:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:domestic financial stability related to aggregate FX exposure, causing policymakers to tighten 
31:1031:83990:21:8:228:231:125:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
31:1032:84045:8:12:70:539:117:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:36 D etailed results are available on request. Each of these estimates are based on regressions using the same format as 
31:1033:84166:12:8:70:477:105:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:the baseline regressions in Tables 1 and 2, including all of the control variables and global time effects. 
31:1034:84273:8:13:70:536:97:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:37  Omitted  variable  bias  is  also  a  frequent  concern  in  cross-country  empirical  papers,  as  some  hard-to-measure 
31:1035:84399:13:10:70:572:84:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:variables could simultaneously affect    cross   -border capital flows and FX regulations. This is less of a concern in our 
31:1036:84523:10:0:70:507:74:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:framework, however, due to the tests for “non-results” corresponding  to our main results (as in   Section IV.B). 
32:1037:84641:0:18:75:530:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations  on banks’  exposure to FX and thereby reduce aggregate FX exposure and/or bank 
32:1038:84733:18:19:75:545:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:lending  in FX.    To  better  control  for  endogeneity,  we  adopt  an  alternative  approach  that 
32:1039:84835:19:19:75:528:669:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:estimates an “exogenous” shock to macroprudential policy, following the   approach used in 
32:1040:84926:19:19:75:528:650:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Auerbach and Gorodnichenko (2013) to  estimate more exogenous fiscal policy shocks and in 
32:1041:85016:19:18:75:547:631:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Furceri et al. (2016) to estimate more exogenous monetary policy shocks. We    estimate a first-
32:1042:85112:18:19:75:538:613:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:stage regression of FX regulations on a range of variables that could affect the implementation  
32:1043:85209:19:19:75:528:594:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:of these regulations. Then,  we use the residuals  from    this regression, which should be a more 
32:1044:85308:19:19:75:528:575:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:exogenous measure of changes in FX regulations, as the explanatory variable in our baseline 
32:1045:85400:19:18:75:528:556:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regressions  (instead  of  using  our -1/0/1  measure  of  changes  in macroprudential FX

33:1084:88788:18:19:75:528:451:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:our main hypotheses. Tighter FX regulation of banks is correlated with banks borrowing less 
33:1085:88880:19:19:75:528:432:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:in  foreign  currency,  with  no  significant  effect  on  their  non-FX  borrowing.  Tighter  FX 
33:1086:88978:19:19:75:548:413:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulation is also    correlated with firms increasing their FX debt issuance, substituting away 
33:1087:89075:19:30:75:471:394:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:from banks, with no significant effect on firms’ and banks’ non-FX debt issuance. 
33:1088:89156:30:19:102:528:364:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Taken  as  a  whole,  these  results  suggest that  FX  regulations  are  successful  in
