34:1106:90721:30:19:102:530:676:115:Georgia:122:Georgia:F:V. Empirical  Results:  Macroprudential  FX Regulations  and  Resilience  to  
34:1107:90798:19:31:75:200:657:122:Georgia:122:Georgia:C:Currency Movements 
34:1108:90816:31:19:102:528:626:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:This section assesses how macroprudential FX regulations on banks affect the exposure 
34:1109:90902:19:18:75:528:607:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:of banks and the broader economy to exchange rate movements. If the primary motivation of 
34:1110:90992:18:19:75:528:589:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:macroprudential  FX  regulations  is  to  reduce  the  vulnerability  of  the  economy  to  sharp 
34:1111:91090:19:19:75:528:570:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:currency  movements,  do  the  regulations  achieve  this  goal?  Does  the  reduction  in  FX 
34:1112:91185:19:19:75:528:551:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:borrowing by banks significantly reduce bank exposure to currency movements? And if so, 
34:1113:91273:19:18:75:528:532:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:through what channels? If bank exposure to currency risk declines, does the exposure largely 
34:1114:91366:18:19:75:528:514:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:shift to other sectors of the economy, so that the aggregate vulnerability of the economy is not 
34:1115:91463:19:31:75:199:495:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:meaningfully improved?  
34:1116:91487:31:19:102:528:464:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:This section attempts to go one step beyond most other work assessing the direct and 
34:1117:91572:19:18:75:528:445:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:spillover effects of macroprudential FX  regulations by also testing if the regulations attain one 
34:1118:91671:18:19:75:528:427:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:of  their  ultimate  goals:  reducing  the  vulnerability  of  the  economy  to  exchange  rate 
34:1119:91767:19:19:75:528:408:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:movements.  As  discussed  in  the  introduction,  there  is  longstanding  evidence  of  the 
34:1120:91861:19:19:75:528:389:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:multifaceted  risks  and  challenges  created  by  exposure  to  currency  movements.  If 
34:1121:91951:19:18:75:528:370:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:macroprudential FX regulations can mitigate these challenges and risks, they could provide 
34:1122:92042:18:19:75:543:352:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:substantive benefits to the broader economy. This approach of testing for the   potential effects 
34:1123:92140:19:19:75:528:333:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:on  country resilience builds  on the    academic  literature  identifying  ways  to  increase  the 
34:1124:92240:19:19:75:528:314:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:effectiveness of regulation in order to strengthen its welfare impact (e.g.,   Nier et al., 2011, 
34:1125:92338:19:30:75:386:295:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Mendicino et al.,  2015, Agénor 2016, and IMF-FSB  -BIS, 2016).  
34:1126:92403:30:31:102:302:265:122:Georgia:122:Georgia:A:A. Empirical Framework and Data

34:1128:92515:19:19:75:528:215:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:macroprudential FX regulations affect the relationship between exchange rate movements

36:1171:96483:0:18:75:528:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations (i.e., an increase in fxmi,t) would reduce exchange rate sensitivity. Since banks are 
36:1172:96581:18:19:75:528:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:directly affected by FX regulation, however, and corporates can switch to market-based FX 
36:1173:96671:19:19:75:528:669:122:g_d0_f2:116:g_d0_f2:B:borrowing and therefore not reduce their foreign currency borrowing by as much as banks, we 
36:1174:96763:19:31:75:466:650:116:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:would expect the coefficient μ to be more negative for banks than for corporates.  
36:1175:96845:31:30:102:198:619:122:Georgia:122:Georgia:A:B. Main Results 
36:1176:96859:30:19:102:533:589:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Table 5  presents  the results on a sample of up to 24 countries over the period 2000Q1 to 
36:1177:96950:19:19:75:542:570:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:2014Q4.45 For most results, we report one set of specifications for   financial stock returns 
36:1178:97044:19:19:75:528:551:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:(representing banks’ stock  returns)  as the dependent  variable  and  another  set  for broad 
36:1179:97139:19:18:75:533:532:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:market  stock  returns  (representing  corporates’  stock  returns).  C olumns  (1)  and  (2)  only 
36:1180:97239:18:19:75:528:514:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:include the three variables central to our exchange rate sensitivity tests, while columns (3) and 
36:1181:97337:19:19:75:528:495:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:(4) add standard controls for equity return regressions (the   baseline). We will focus on the 
36:1182:97432:19:19:75:525:476:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:first three variables in each column: the cumulated FX regulation measure; the financially-
36:1183:97523:19:18:75:528:457:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:weighted exchange rate (defined so that positive is an appreciation of the domestic currency); 
36:1184:97618:18:19:75:528:439:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:and  their  interaction.  The  signs  of  the  other  control  variables  are  generally  similar  for 
36:1185:97721:19:19:75:528:420:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:financials  and  the  broad  market indices and  have  the  expected  signs,  albeit  some  have 
36:1186:97818:19:31:75:202:401:122:g_d0_f2:116:g_d0_f2:B:fluctuating significance.46 
36:1187:97845:31:18:102:532:370:116:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:In each of the specifications in columns (1) -  (4), the coefficients on FX regulations  are 
36:1188:97938:18:19:75:528:352:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:insignificant—albeit  usually  negative  and  larger  for  financials—possibly  indicating  that 
36:1189:98035:19:19:75:528:333:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:increased macroprudential FX regulations on banks could reduce bank stock returns. The 
36:1190:98122:19:19:75:528:314:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:coefficient  on  the  exchange rate  is  positive  and  significant  in  each  case,  suggesting  that 
36:1191:98225:19:30:75:499:295:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:currency appreciation corresponds to higher stock returns (as predicted in the model).  
36:1192:98313:30:19:102:528:265:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Most important for our analysis, the coefficient on the interaction term (the coefficient 
36:1193:98403:19:19:75:543:246:122:g_d0_f5:122:g_d0_f2:B:μ in equations (17) and (18))   is negative in each of the four columns. This suggests that 
36:1194:98495:19:19:75:528:227:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:increased macroprudential FX regulations reduce the sensitivity of banks and corporates to 
36:1195:98586:19:18:75:528:208:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:exchange rate movements. This coefficient, however, is only negative and significant at the 5% 
36:1196:98681:18:19:75:528:190:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:level for bank returns (columns (1) and (3)), and the estimated magnitude of the coefficient is 
36:1197:98777:19:26:75:528:171:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:over 50% larger for banks than corporates in each case. This suggests that macroprudential 
36:1198:98868:26:8:228:231:145:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:

36:1200:99042:13:10:70:537:124:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:returns variable. The countries for which data is available for this analysis are: Australia, Austria, Brazil, Canada, Czech 
36:1201:99166:10:10:70:536:114:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:Republic, Denmark, Hong Kong SAR, Hungary, India, Indonesia, Korea, Malaysia, Mexico, New Zealand, Norway,

36:1203:99374:8:13:70:537:96:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:46 For example, higher stock returns are correlated with higher industry production growth, lower inflation, a reduction 
36:1204:99495:13:0:70:402:83:81:g_d0_f2:77:g_d0_f2:?:in interest rates, higher stock market turnover, and a lower level of global volatility. 
37:1205:99587:0:18:75:528:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:FX regulations reduce banks’ sensitivity to exchange rate movements more than that for the 
37:1206:99678:18:31:75:235:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:broader economy—as predicted. 
37:1207:99707:31:19:102:534:657:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:The magnitudes  of the coefficients in Table 5  also provide more information on the size 
37:1208:99797:19:19:75:532:638:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:of these effects. Focusing on the columns with the full set of controls in  columns (3) and (4), 
37:1209:99894:19:18:75:528:619:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:when the cumulated   measures of macroprudential FX regulation is neutral, a 1 percentage 
37:1210:99984:18:19:75:528:601:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:point  depreciation  in the  financially-weighted  exchange  rate  leads  to  a  decrease  in stock 
37:1211:100084:19:19:75:528:582:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:market returns for financials by 1.46 percentage points and for the broad market by 1.18 
37:1212:100173:19:19:75:534:563:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:per centage points. When FX regulations are tightened, the same depreciation corresponds to 
37:1213:100265:19:18:75:528:544:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:a 0.67 percentage point decline in returns for financials and 0.75 percentage point decline for 
37:1214:100361:18:19:75:528:526:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:the broader market. Hence, tighter macroprudential FX regulations reduce the sensitivity of 
37:1215:100453:19:19:75:528:507:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:stock returns to exchange rate shocks for both banks and the broader economy, but the effect 
37:1216:100546:19:31:75:407:488:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:is  almost twice as large    for banks (and insignificant for corporates).  
37:1217:100622:31:18:102:528:457:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Next, since     the broad market index is only a rough proxy for corporate stock returns (as 
37:1218:100715:18:19:75:529:439:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:this   includes banks as well as non-bank financial institutions), column (5) shows results when 
37:1219:100812:19:19:75:533:420:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:an artificially-constructed measure of corporate stock returns  is used instead of the broad 
37:1220:100905:19:19:75:534:401:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:market index. This proxy is calculated by regressing the broad market return index on  the 
37:1221:100996:19:18:75:528:382:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:financial  return  index  and  taking  the  residual. This  should  better  isolate  the  impact  on 
37:1222:101097:18:19:75:528:364:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:corporate returns—but should be interpreted cautiously as this regression could also remove 
37:1223:101189:19:19:75:528:345:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:the effects of any omitted variables that affect both corporate and financial stock returns. With 
37:1224:101287:19:19:75:528:326:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:this  caveat,  the  estimates  support  the  model’s  predictions  that  FX  macroprudential 
37:1225:101380:19:18:75:528:307:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations reduce corporate sensitivity to exchange rate movements by less than that for 
37:1226:101470:18:19:75:528:289:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:banks. More specifically, the coefficient on the interaction term between FX regulation and 
37:1227:101562:19:19:75:528:270:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:the exchange rate is insignificant and positive—a sharp contrast to the negative and significant 
37:1228:101659:19:19:75:528:251:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:coefficient for the financial index, as well as to the negative and sometimes weakly significant 
37:1229:101756:19:18:75:528:232:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:coefficient for the broad index. Since the coefficient estimate is insignificant, we are cautious 
37:1230:101854:18:19:75:528:214:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:about interpreting the sign of the effect on corporates—but instead can conclude that this 
37:1231:101945:19:19:75:528:195:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:result suggests any effect of macroprudential regulations on the sensitivity of corporates to 
37:1232:102039:19:40:75:339:176:122:g_d0_f2:116:g_d0_f2:B:exchange rate movements is small and insignificant.47 
37:1233:102092:40:8:228:231:136:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
37:1234:102147:8:13:70:537:128:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:47 It is also possible, however, that these estimates understate the reduction in FX exposure due to the differential 
37:1235:102265:13:10:70:536:115:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:impact  on  small  firms.  More  specifically,  smaller  firms  are  more  likely  to  rely  on  banks  for  funding,  and  if  FX 
37:1236:102396:10:11:70:537:105:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:regulations cause banks to reduce their FX   lending to these smaller firms, these firms may be unable to issue debt on 
37:1237:102516:11:10:70:535:94:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:international markets. These smaller firms would therefore be forced to reduce their FX borrowing and exposure—
37:1238:102627:10:10:70:536:84:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:whether by shifting to local currency borrowing or not borrowing at all. These effects would not be captured in the 
37:1239:102743:10:0:70:495:74:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:empirical analysis as these smaller firms are also less likely to be included as part as the main equity index. 
38:1240:102858:0:18:102:528:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:The  final four columns  of  Table 5   further  explore  this  relationship between 
38:1241:102942:18:19:75:528:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:macroprudential FX  regulations  and  sensitivity  to  exchange  rate  movements under  two 
38:1242:103034:19:19:75:528:669:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:scenarios when the impact of exchange rate movements on stock returns is expected to be 
38:1243:103122:19:19:75:546:650:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:large   r than average: for emerging markets (which tend to have greater exposure to FX) and 
38:1244:103215:19:18:75:528:631:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:for larger exchange rate movements. An extensive literature focuses on the greater sensitivity

38:1248:103592:19:18:75:547:556:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:suggested that the impact of exchange rate movements on the economy may be non-   linear 
38:1249:103681:18:19:75:544:538:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:and greater after large movements, especially depreciations (e.g. ,  Kappler et al. 2013  )— so

38:1251:103876:19:19:75:528:500:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:movements in the exchange rate below the 10th percentile and above the 90th percentile. In 
38:1252:103967:19:18:75:525:481:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:both of these scenarios, the key signs and significance from the base case remain unchanged—
38:1253:104059:18:19:75:528:463:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:but the estimated magnitudes of the coefficients are all larger. For example, and most relevant 
38:1254:104155:19:19:75:535:444:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:to  this  paper’s  analysis,  tighter  macroprudential FX  regulations  correspond  to  a  greater 
38:1255:104254:19:19:75:528:425:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:reduction in the exchange rate sensitivity of emerging markets, and to all countries after large 
38:1256:104351:19:30:75:363:406:122:g_d0_f2:116:g_d0_f2:B:exchange rate movements, than occurs for the full sample.

38:1269:105493:32:30:111:492:124:144:Georgia:144:Georgia:C:C. The Channels Through Which FX Regulations A ffect Banks 
38:1270:105550:30:19:116:538:94:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:The  last  section has  shown  that  macroprudential  FX  regulations  correspond  to  a 
38:1271:105639:19:0:84:541:75:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:significant reduction in the sensitivity of bank stock returns to exchange rate movements;  but 
39:1272:105739:0:18:84:538:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:how    does  this  occur?  This  section  provides  some  initial  evidence,  focusing  on  the key 
39:1273:105839:18:19:84:558:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:mechanisms  suggested in the theoretical model and    for which data for our cross   -section of 
39:1274:105936:19:19:84:538:669:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:countries (particularly emerging markets) is available. Specifically, Section II.C. highlights 
39:1275:106030:19:32:84:491:650:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:three channels through which FX regulations could affect banks’ lending outcomes: 
39:1276:106111:32:18:107:550:618:122:g_d0_f10:122:g_d0_f2:?:• The lending rate that banks charge to their customers increases, due   to the tax from 
39:1277:106199:18:20:85:169:600:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:the regulations . 
39:1278:106217:20:19:107:538:580:122:g_d0_f10:122:g_d0_f2:?:• The   number of firms that borrow from banks declines, because the associated rise in 
39:1279:106304:19:19:85:536:561:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:borrowing costs forces low productivity firms to shift from bank funding to investor funding. 
39:1280:106398:19:19:107:538:542:122:g_d0_f10:122:g_d0_f2:?:• The share of non-performing bank loans falls, because low productivity firms borrow 
39:1281:106483:19:31:85:444:523:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:less from banks, thereby reducing banks’ shares of low-quality borrowers. 
39:1282:106557:31:19:116:537:492:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:Table 6  reports empirical evidence on these three effects using annual data.48 For each 
39:1283:106646:19:18:84:537:473:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:test, we report two results: the coefficient from a regression of the variable of interest on 
39:1284:106740:18:19:84:537:455:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:changes in FX regulations (as defined above) with country and time fixed effects, and then the 
39:1285:106835:19:19:84:537:436:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:same  specification  with  additional  time-varying  controls  for  each  country’s business  and 
39:1286:106933:19:31:84:474:417:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:financial cycle (captured by real GDP growth and credit growth, respectively).    
39:1287:107015:31:18:116:538:386:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:Columns (1) and (2) report results for the relationship between FX regulations and 
39:1288:107098:18:19:84:537:368:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:banks’ risk-adjusted lending rate.  Both  coefficients on the FX measures are positive and 
39:1289:107189:19:19:84:538:349:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:significant (at least at the 10% level), as expected; a tightening of FX regulations makes lending 
39:1290:107288:19:19:84:537:330:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:more expensive and increases the lending rate that banks charge to their customers. Next, 
39:1291:107378:19:19:84:556:311:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Columns  (3)  and  (4) report  results  for  the  relationship  between FX  regulations and    the 
39:1292:107477:19:18:85:538:292:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:number  of  borrowers  from  banks. Both  coefficients  are  negative (as  expected), but 
39:1293:107567:18:19:84:557:274:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:insignificant.49 Columns (5) and (6) assess the relationship with    the share of banks’ non-
39:1294:107660:19:19:84:538:255:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:performing loans. Both    coefficients on FX regulations are again negative, as expected, and 
39:1295:107754:19:18:84:552:236:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:significant (at least at the 10% level). This supports the prediction that tighter FX   regulations 
39:1296:107854:18:31:84:295:218:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:reduce the  share of non-performing loans.  
39:1297:107897:31:19:116:538:187:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:All in all, these results provide additional support for the key mechanisms highlighted 
39:1298:107985:19:19:84:537:168:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:in the theoretical model on how tighter macroprudential FX regulations affect banks. These 
39:1299:108076:19:18:84:538:149:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:also provide additional support for how    these regulations could reduce bank sensitivity to 
39:1300:108170:18:25:84:538:131:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:currency movements—by reducing the share of loans made to the low productivity firms that 
39:1301:108260:25:9:228:231:106:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
39:1302:108315:9:10:70:360:97:42:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:48 See  Appendix A for more information on data definitions and sources. 
39:1303:108386:10:13:70:537:87:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:49 When the analysis is repeated with only FX measures targeting bank assets, both coefficients remain negative and 
39:1304:108502:13:0:70:215:74:81:g_d0_f2:99:g_d0_f2:?:become significant (at the 5% level). 
40:1305:108543:0:18:84:535:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:are  more  sensitive  to  currency  movements,  and  therefore  reducing  banks’  share  of  non-
40:1306:108640:18:19:84:537:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:performing loans. These results are not definitive empirical tests, however, and should simply 
40:1307:108735:19:19:84:551:669:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:be  interpreted  as conditional  correlations which provide  supporting  evidence for   the  key 
40:1308:108832:19:31:84:301:650:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:channels highlighted throughout this paper. 
40:1309:108875:31:30:116:119:619:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C: 
40:1310:108875:30:31:102:193:589:115:Georgia:122:Georgia:A:VI. Conclusions 
40:1311:108889:31:19:102:528:558:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:A growing literature is beginning to document how macroprudential tools can improve 
40:1312:108973:19:19:75:528:539:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:financial stability and reduce the amplification of systemic risk. This literature, however, is 
40:1313:109069:19:18:75:528:520:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:also  beginning  to  document  how  these  tools  often  have  unintended  consequences.  One 
40:1314:109163:18:19:75:540:502:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:macroprudential tool which is be  coming more widely utilized, but has   received relatively less 
40:1315:109261:19:19:75:528:483:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:attention in academic research, is regulations on FX exposure. This is despite longstanding 
40:1316:109353:19:31:75:519:464:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:evidence that foreign currency exposure can generate important economic vulnerabilities .  
40:1317:109444:31:18:102:528:433:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:This  paper  attempts  to  address  this  gap  by  analyzing  the  incidence  and  impact  of 
40:1318:109538:18:19:75:528:415:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:macroprudential FX regulations. It develops the key concepts in a theoretical model, compiles 
40:1319:109632:19:19:75:528:396:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:a dataset with detailed information on these regulations over time, and then uses it to test the 
40:1320:109729:19:19:75:528:377:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:predictions of the model. The results show that after an increase in macroprudential FX 
40:1321:109817:19:18:75:528:358:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulations: (1) banks borrow and lend less in foreign currency (with no change in their 
40:1322:109906:18:19:75:535:340:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:borrowing in local currency); (2) firms shift    away from bank FX  borrowing and increase their 
40:1323:110003:19:19:75:528:321:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:FX borrowing from market investors (with no increase in firm and bank non-FX borrowing 
40:1324:110090:19:19:75:528:302:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:from  investors);  (3)  banks  are  less  exposed  to  exchange  rate  movements;  and  (4)  firms 
40:1325:110189:19:18:75:528:283:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:experience some reduction in their exposure to exchange rate movements, but less than for 
40:1326:110279:18:19:75:528:265:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:banks. Each of these results supports the main predictions of the model. This combination of 
40:1327:110372:19:19:75:528:246:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:results suggests that even if macroprudential FX regulations on banks accomplish their direct 
40:1328:110466:19:19:75:528:227:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:goals and significantly  reduc   e  bank vulnerability to currency movements, they also generate 
40:1329:110563:19:18:75:535:208:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:meaningful leakages and partially “shift the snowbanks” of FX  vulnerability to other sectors 
40:1330:110657:18:31:75:156:190:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:of the economy. 
40:1331:110672:31:19:102:528:159:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Although these empirical results are robust to a number of extensions and sensitivity 
40:1332:110758:19:19:75:528:140:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:tests, several caveats are important. The underlying data on foreign currency borrowing may 
40:1333:110850:19:18:75:528:121:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:miss important aspects of bank and firm FX exposures. For example, the data includes limited 
40:1334:110942:18:19:75:528:103:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:information on firm or bank exposure to foreign currency that occurs without crossing borders 
40:1335:111036:19:0:75:528:84:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:(such as if a local household makes a bank deposit in foreign currency). The data also does not 
41:1336:111136:0:18:75:528:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:incorporate any transactions or changes in exposure that occur entirely through trading or 
41:1337:111227:18:19:75:532:688:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:lending in a third country (as often occurs in financial centers).  Moreover, the analysis does 
41:1338:111323:19:19:75:528:669:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:not include information on hedging—whether natural or in financial markets—which could 
41:1339:111410:19:19:75:528:650:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:reduce an entity’s  vulnerability to currency movements even if it has large gross FX positions. 
41:1340:111507:19:18:75:528:631:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Many of these data challenges, however, might be expected to bias estimates toward zero, 
41:1341:111596:18:19:75:528:613:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:thereby suggesting some of the effects estimated in the paper could actually be larger if better 
41:1342:111693:19:19:75:528:594:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:data existed. For example, if firms respond to tighter FX regulations at home by issuing FX 
41:1343:111785:19:19:75:548:575:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:debt abroad and selling it to a foreigner ( with    the entire transaction in London),    this leakage 
41:1344:111888:19:30:75:263:556:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:would not be captured in our analysis. 
41:1345:111926:30:19:102:526:526:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:Another important caveat is that the analysis in this paper does not provide a full cost-
41:1346:112015:19:19:75:528:507:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:benefit calculation of the impact of macroprudential regulations—either in the theoretical 
41:1347:112106:19:19:75:528:488:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:model or the empirical analysis. Macroprudential regulations can have much broader costs 
41:1348:112195:19:18:75:529:469:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:and benefits than those explored in this paper—such as on the distortions created as firms, 
41:1349:112287:18:19:75:528:451:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:banks and individuals find other ways to reduce the impact of the regulations (perhaps by 
41:1350:112376:19:19:75:528:432:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:shifting business to other countries with a different regulatory framework). A full test of these 
41:1351:112474:19:19:75:528:413:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:various effects is beyond the scope of this paper—but would be a promising avenue for future 
41:1352:112567:19:30:75:388:394:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:work (with datasets better targeted to address these questions).  
41:1353:112632:30:19:102:529:364:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:With  these  caveats,  the  results in  this  paper have  important  implications  for  the 
41:1354:112724:19:19:75:529:345:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:application  of  macroprudential  policy. One   key  implication  is  for  the  debate  on  capital 
41:1355:112824:19:19:75:529:326:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:controls versus macroprudential policy. Countries concerned about excessive borrowing in 
41:1356:112913:19:18:75:528:307:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:foreign currency may consider capital controls (especially for bank borrowing in FX, which is 
41:1357:113007:18:19:75:528:289:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:particularly volatile and linked to booms and busts50). Macroprudential regulations on banks, 
41:1358:113101:19:19:75:528:270:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:however, appear to be effective in reducing this vulnerability in the financial system without 
41:1359:113196:19:19:75:528:251:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:resorting to capital controls—controls which are illegal in some contexts (such as for EU 
41:1360:113286:19:18:75:552:232:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:members and in some trade agreements). A  lthough macroprudential bank     regulations can 
41:1361:113377:18:19:75:532:214:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:also    generate leakages (such as an increase in FX debt issuance by corporates),  capital controls 
41:1362:113478:19:19:75:528:195:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:can also generate costs    and unintended consequences—including other ways of “shifting the 
41:1363:113571:19:51:76:370:176:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:sno wbank” of FX risks to different sectors of the economy.51  
41:1364:113634:51:8:228:231:125:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
41:1365:113689:8:10:70:190:117:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:50 See Hoggarth et al. (2016).  
41:1366:113721:10:13:70:532:107:36:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:F:51 For example, Keller (2018) shows that capital controls can cause banks to increase FX lending to domestic firms 
41:1367:113836:13:10:70:532:94:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:F:(in order to better hedge their foreign currency deposits when international hedging becomes more expensive), 
41:1368:113946:10:10:70:532:84:81:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:F:thereby causing an increase in the  foreign currency exposure of domestic companies. For other evidence on the costs 
41:1369:114063:10:0:70:318:74:81:g_d0_f2:99:g_d0_f2:?:and distortions created by capital controls, see Forbes (2007). 
42:1370:114129:0:30:102:105:706:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A: 
42:1371:114129:30:19:102:528:676:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:A:A  final set  of implications  for  the  application  of  macroprudential  policies is  the 
42:1372:114221:19:19:75:528:657:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:importance  of  the regulatory  perimeter and  implications  for  aggregate  welfare  if 
42:1373:114310:19:19:75:528:638:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:macroprudential policies partially shift risks from the regulated sector to unregulated sectors. 
42:1374:114407:19:18:75:525:619:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:Our results suggest that macroprudential FX regulations can reduce risks in a systemically-
42:1375:114498:18:19:75:528:601:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:important sector of the economy (banks). This needs  to be balanced, however, against any 
42:1376:114588:19:19:75:528:582:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:increase  in risks  in  other  sectors which are  in  the  “shadow”  and  potentially  less  well 
42:1377:114686:19:19:75:528:563:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:understood than those in the regulated sector.52 Are these shadow investors less informed 
42:1378:114774:19:20:75:529:544:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:and/or  less  able  to  manage  exchange  rate  movements  than  banks? Do the  regulations 
42:1379:114866:20:19:75:534:524:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:generate other costs, such as by  reducing output due to the less efficient allocation of FX 
42:1380:114959:19:19:75:528:505:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:lending by investors which lack the knowledge from banks’ screening activities? Even if the 
42:1381:115051:19:18:75:528:486:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:overall  FX  exposure  of  the  economy  falls,  does  this  benefit  outweigh  other  costs  of  the 
42:1382:115153:18:19:75:528:468:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:regulation?  Just  as  a  fresh  snowbank  rarely  stays  white  for  long,  the  impact  of 
42:1383:115246:19:31:75:431:449:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:B:macroprudential regulation on country resilience can quickly get muddy. 
42:1384:115317:31:12:84:87:418:122:Georgia:122:Georgia:A: 
42:1385:115317:12:310:228:231:406:122:Georgia:122:Georgia:C:  
42:1386:115317:310:9:228:231:96:122:g_d0_f2:122:g_d0_f2:C:                                                        
42:1387:115372:9:13:70:542:87:42:g_d0_f2:81:g_d0_f2:?:52 Bengui and Bianchi (2014) explore this question in a  model of the impact of capital controls, a model which finds 
42:1388:115489:13:0:70:464:74:81:g_d0_f2:99:g_d0_f2:?:that the controls reduce risk on regulated agents but increase risk taking in the “shadow” economy.
